Trainer based in Glasgow</strong>, bringing over a decade of professional experience to the assessment and treatment of dog behaviour issues.</p><p data-start="1214" data-end="1469">A Full Member of the Association of Pet Behaviour Counsellors<strong> (<a href="https://www.apbc.org.uk/find-an-apbc-member/">APBC</a>)</strong> and a <strong data-start="917" data-end="1012">Registered Clinical Animal Behaviourist </strong>with the Animal Behaviour &amp; Training Council<strong data-start="917" data-end="1012"> (<a href="https://abtc.org.uk/">ABTC</a>)</strong>, Jim is also an <strong><a href="https://iaabc.org/en/">IAABC</a> </strong>Certified Dog Behaviour Consultant (CDBC)<strong>.</strong> Jim works with dogs presenting with a wide range of behaviour challenges, including aggression, anxiety, fears &amp; phobias, and reactivity.</p><p>Fully qualified and accredited, Jim carries comprehensive professional insurance. Over the course of his career, he has supported thousands of dogs through one-to-one behaviour work.</p><p><strong data-start="1357" data-end="1389">CBT Dog Behaviour &amp; Training</strong> was awarded <em data-start="1402" data-end="1458">Canine Behaviour Specialist of the Year 2025 – Glasgow</em> and <em data-start="1463" data-end="1500">Best Dog Behaviour Consultancy 2025</em> at the Scottish Enterprise Awards.</p><p>On this site, you can enjoy Jim&#8217;s professional insights in the <a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/dog-behaviourist-glasgow-blog/">blog</a> and <a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/animal-behaviour-podcast/">podcast,</a> where current, evidence-based approaches to behaviour assessment and intervention are discussed.</p><p>Jim specialises in addressing a wide range of behaviour issues, including:</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_divider et_pb_divider_0 et_pb_divider_position_ et_pb_space"><div et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_text_inner"><h1 id='submit-an-enquiry'  id="boomdevs_8" style="text-align: center;">Submit an Enquiry</h1></div></div><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_text et_pb_text_9  et_pb_text_align_left et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_text_inner"><p style="text-align: center;"><strong>Use this form to share some initial details about your dog and the concerns you’re experiencing. et_pb_blurb_position_top et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_blurb_content"><div class="et_pb_main_blurb_image"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/dogs-behaving-very-badly-a-review/" target="_blank"><span class="et_pb_image_wrap et_pb_only_image_mode_wrap"><img decoding="async" data-src="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/DALL·E-2023-10-18-11.29.34-Photo-of-a-husky-with-a-focused-gaze-looking-directly-at-a-TV-screen-placed-in-front-of-it.-The-TV-screen-distinctly-and-solely-displays-the-text-Do.jpg" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB3aWR0aD0iMSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxIiB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciPjwvc3ZnPg==" style="--smush-placeholder-width: 1024px; --smush-placeholder-aspect-ratio: 1024/576;" /></span></a></div><div class="et_pb_blurb_container"><h4 class="et_pb_module_header"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/dogs-behaving-very-badly-a-review/" target="_blank">Dogs Behaving (Very) Badly – A Review</a></h4><div class="et_pb_blurb_description"><p>Television shows like “Dogs Behaving (Very) Badly” have a significant impact on dog owners’ perception of their pets’ behaviour and their approach to addressing problems or unwanted behaviours. As dog trainers on TV are often the primary source of information for the general public, it is crucial that they provide accurate and up-to-date advice on dog training and behaviour management.</p></div></div></div></div></div><div class="et_pb_column et_pb_column_1_3 et_pb_column_23  et_pb_css_mix_blend_mode_passthrough"><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_blurb et_pb_blurb_8 et_clickable  et_pb_text_align_left  et_pb_blurb_position_top et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_blurb_content"><div class="et_pb_main_blurb_image"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/is-aggression-genetic-or-learned/" target="_blank"><span class="et_pb_image_wrap et_pb_only_image_mode_wrap"><img decoding="async" data-src="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/DALL·E-2023-10-17-19.59.11-Photo-of-diverse-dogs-in-a-park-displaying-various-behaviors.-A-DNA-helix-is-superimposed-over-the-scene-hinting-at-genetic-factors.-In-the-backgrou.png" alt="Photo of diverse dogs in a park, displaying various behaviors. A DNA helix is superimposed over the scene" class="et-waypoint et_pb_animation_off et_pb_animation_off_tablet et_pb_animation_off_phone lazyload" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB3aWR0aD0iMSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxIiB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciPjwvc3ZnPg==" style="--smush-placeholder-width: 1792px; --smush-placeholder-aspect-ratio: 1792/1024;" /></span></a></div><div class="et_pb_blurb_container"><h4 class="et_pb_module_header"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/is-aggression-genetic-or-learned/" target="_blank">Is Aggression Genetic or Learned?</a></h4><div class="et_pb_blurb_description"><p><span>Aggression in dogs is a complex behaviour influenced by both genetic and environmental factors. While some breeds may have a genetic predisposition to aggression, it can occur in any breed. Factors like socialisation, training, and past experiences impact a dog’s behaviour. Aggression is both genetic and learned, with genes providing the foundation and environmental factors shaping the expression of the behaviour. </span></p></div></div></div></div></div><div class="et_pb_column et_pb_column_1_3 et_pb_column_24  et_pb_css_mix_blend_mode_passthrough et-last-child"><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_blurb et_pb_blurb_9 et_clickable  et_pb_text_align_left  et_pb_blurb_position_top et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_blurb_content"><div class="et_pb_main_blurb_image"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/sudden-onset-aggression-rage-syndrome/" target="_blank"><span class="et_pb_image_wrap et_pb_only_image_mode_wrap"><img decoding="async" data-src="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/DALL·E-2023-10-19-09.31.32-Photo-of-a-diverse-group-of-concerned-dog-owners-gathered-around-a-veterinarian-who-is-pointing-to-a-clear-and-legible-chart-detailing-the-causes-and-.png" alt="Photo of a diverse group of concerned dog owners gathered around a veterinarian who is pointing to a clear and legible chart detailing the causes" class="et-waypoint et_pb_animation_off et_pb_animation_off_tablet et_pb_animation_off_phone lazyload" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB3aWR0aD0iMSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxIiB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciPjwvc3ZnPg==" style="--smush-placeholder-width: 1792px; --smush-placeholder-aspect-ratio: 1792/1024;" /></span></a></div><div class="et_pb_blurb_container"><h4 class="et_pb_module_header"><a href="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/sudden-onset-aggression-rage-syndrome/" target="_blank">Rage Syndrome in Dogs</a></h4><div class="et_pb_blurb_description"><p><span>Rage Syndrome in dogs is a debated phenomenon involving sudden and unprovoked aggressive behaviour. Its causes may include genetics, neurological abnormalities, hormonal imbalances, and environmental factors. Diagnosing it is challenging, as there’s no specific test, but it often involves medical examinations and behavioural assessments. Treatment may include medication, behaviour modification, and environmental changes</span></p></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="et_pb_bottom_inside_divider et-no-transition"></div></div><div class="et_pb_section et_pb_section_8 et_section_regular" ><div class="et_pb_row et_pb_row_13"><div class="et_pb_column et_pb_column_4_4 et_pb_column_25  et_pb_css_mix_blend_mode_passthrough et-last-child"><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_image et_pb_image_5"> <span class="et_pb_image_wrap "><img decoding="async" width="203" height="202" data-src="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/logo.png" alt="" title="logo" data-srcset="https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/logo.png 203w, https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/logo-100x100.png 100w, https://cbtdogbehaviour.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/logo-150x150.png 150w" data-sizes="(max-width: 203px) 100vw, 203px" class="wp-image-111409 lazyload" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB3aWR0aD0iMSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxIiB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciPjwvc3ZnPg==" style="--smush-placeholder-width: 203px; --smush-placeholder-aspect-ratio: 203/202;" /></span></div><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_text et_pb_text_31  et_pb_text_align_center et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_text_inner"><p>FAQs</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_text et_pb_text_32  et_pb_text_align_left et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_text_inner"><h3 id='frequently-asked-questions'  id="boomdevs_17" style="text-align: center;">Frequently Asked Questions</h3></div></div><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_text et_pb_text_33  et_pb_text_align_center et_pb_bg_layout_light"><div class="et_pb_text_inner"><p>Some commonly asked questions</p></div></div></div></div><div class="et_pb_row et_pb_row_14 et_pb_equal_columns et_pb_gutters2"><div class="et_pb_column et_pb_column_1_2 et_pb_column_26  et_pb_css_mix_blend_mode_passthrough"><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_accordion et_pb_accordion_0"><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_0  et_pb_toggle_open"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">What is a dog behaviourist?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p>A dog behaviourist is a qualified professional who assesses and treats behaviour problems by identifying the emotional, environmental, and sometimes medical factors influencing a dog’s behaviour. Clinical behaviourists work with both the dog and their guardian to develop a structured, evidence-based behaviour modification plan, and may liaise with veterinary professionals where appropriate.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_1  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">What kind of issues can a dog behaviourist help with?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">A dog behaviourist can help with a wide range of behaviour concerns, including aggression towards dogs or people, anxiety-related behaviour, separation-related distress, fear-based behaviour and phobias, reactivity, compulsive or repetitive behaviours, excessive barking, and more complex or persistent behaviour problems. Support may also be appropriate where behaviour has changed following illness, injury, or ongoing pain.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_2  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">How do I know if I need a dog behaviourist?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">You may benefit from working with a dog behaviourist if your dog’s behaviour is causing distress, poses a safety concern, is worsening over time, or has not improved with basic training approaches. Behaviour support is also recommended where behaviour appears linked to fear, anxiety, aggression, or other underlying factors rather than simple training gaps.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_3  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">What happens during a dog behaviour consultation?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">A behaviour consultation involves a detailed discussion of your dog’s history, environment, and current behaviour, alongside observation where appropriate. The aim is to understand why the behaviour is occurring and what factors may be maintaining it. Following the consultation, you will receive a written behaviour report and a personalised behaviour modification plan, with follow-up support offered where needed.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_4  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">Is there a guarantee that my dog&#039;s behaviour will change?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p data-start="2183" data-end="2527">There is no ethical guarantee of behaviour change. Progress depends on many factors, including the nature of the behaviour, the dog’s emotional state, environmental influences, and consistency in implementing recommendations. The focus of behaviour work is on improving welfare, safety, and quality of life through realistic, achievable change.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="et_pb_column et_pb_column_1_2 et_pb_column_27  et_pb_css_mix_blend_mode_passthrough et-last-child"><div class="et_pb_module et_pb_accordion et_pb_accordion_1"><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_5  et_pb_toggle_open"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">How many sessions will it take to modify my dog&#039;s behaviour?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p>The number of sessions required varies from case to case. Some situations benefit from a single consultation and written guidance, while others require ongoing support over a longer period. This will depend on the complexity of the behaviour, contributing factors, and how the plan is implemented in daily life.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_6  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">How much does a dog behaviour consultation cost?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">Costs vary depending on the level of support required. Clear pricing for behaviour consultations and support packages is provided in advance, and recommendations are made based on the needs of the individual case. Insurance-funded options may be available where appropriate.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_7  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">Can a dog behaviourist help with all breeds of dogs?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">Yes. Behaviour work is based on the individual dog, their history, environment, and emotional needs, rather than breed alone. Support is tailored to each dog and household, taking breed traits into account where relevant.</p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_8  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">How do I book a consultation with a dog behaviourist?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;"><span>To book a consultation with a dog behaviourist, simply <strong>enquire now</strong> to schedule an appointment. It is important to provide as much information as possible about your dog&#8217;s behaviour to ensure that the consultation is as effective as possible.</span></p></div></div><div class="et_pb_toggle et_pb_module et_pb_accordion_item et_pb_accordion_item_9  et_pb_toggle_close"><h4 class="et_pb_toggle_title">Do I need a veterinary referral to work with a clinical animal behaviourist?</h4><div class="et_pb_toggle_content clearfix"><p style="font-weight: 400;">In some cases, veterinary involvement is recommended to rule out or address medical factors that may influence behaviour. Where appropriate, collaboration with your vet forms part of a safe, ethical, and welfare-led approach.</p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></article></div><footer class="et-l
